  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer12134203408049224524">«في التائهون، أستلهم فترة شبابي بتصرف شديد. فقد عشتُ تلك الفترة مع أصدقاء كانوا يؤمنون بعالم أفضل. ومع أنَّ لا شبه بين أبطال هذه الرواية وبين أشخاص حقيقيين، فهم ليسوا من نسج الخيال تماماً. فلقد نهلتُ من معين أحلامي واستيهاماتي وحسراتي بقدر ما نهلتُ من معين ذكرياتي». <br/>كان أبطال هذه الرواية متلازمين في شبابهم ثم تشتَّتوا ودبَّ بينهم الخصام وفرّقتهم الأيام، وسيجتمع شملهم بمناس</span>
  <span id="freeText12134203408049224524" style="display:none">«في التائهون، أستلهم فترة شبابي بتصرف شديد. فقد عشتُ تلك الفترة مع أصدقاء كانوا يؤمنون بعالم أفضل. ومع أنَّ لا شبه بين أبطال هذه الرواية وبين أشخاص حقيقيين، فهم ليسوا من نسج الخيال تماماً. فلقد نهلتُ من معين أحلامي واستيهاماتي وحسراتي بقدر ما نهلتُ من معين ذكرياتي». <br />كان أبطال هذه الرواية متلازمين في شبابهم ثم تشتَّتوا ودبَّ بينهم الخصام وفرّقتهم الأيام، وسيجتمع شملهم بمناسبة وفاة أحدهم. بعضهم أبى أن يغادر وطنه الأم، وبعضهم الآخر هاجر إلى الولايات المتحدة، أو البرازيل، أو فرنسا، وأخذتهم الدروب التي سلكوها في اتجاهات مختلفة. فماذا يجمع بعد بين صاحبة الفندق المتحرِّرة، أو المقاول الذي جمع ثروة، أو الراهب الذي اعتزل العالم وانصرف إلى التأمل؟ بعض الذكريات المشتركة، وحنين لا برء منه للزمن الذي مضى.</span>

<div id="review_1929496276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1929496276" />
    <a title="Medhat The Book Fanatic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17165680-medhat-the-book-fanatic"><img alt="Medhat The Book Fanatic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580998140p2/17165680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1929496276?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Medhat The Book Fanatic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Medhat The Book Fanatic" href="/user/show/17165680-medhat-the-book-fanatic">Medhat The Book Fanatic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17165680-medhat-the-book-fanatic?shelf=books-read-in-2017">books-read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1929496276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14398714520363581938">Technically, 4.5 stars for The Disoriented Ones by Lebanese author Amin Maalouf.<br/><br/>A friendship between 7 college students is shattered when the Lebanese Civil War begins and life takes them on different paths over 4 continents. <br/><br/>A quarter Century later, Adam, our main protagonist and narrator, who lives in France, is called by his old friend Murad (and his wife Tania, one of the old friends), who is dying from cancer, and asks to see him on his deathbed for one last time, to seek forgiveness from A</span>
  <span id="freeText14398714520363581938" style="display:none">Technically, 4.5 stars for The Disoriented Ones by Lebanese author Amin Maalouf.<br /><br />A friendship between 7 college students is shattered when the Lebanese Civil War begins and life takes them on different paths over 4 continents. <br /><br />A quarter Century later, Adam, our main protagonist and narrator, who lives in France, is called by his old friend Murad (and his wife Tania, one of the old friends), who is dying from cancer, and asks to see him on his deathbed for one last time, to seek forgiveness from Adam over an old bad affair. <br /><br />At first, he refuses to go, but after second thoughts and a push from his partner, Adam accepts. Afterwards, he will find out that his friend has died on the dawn of his arrival to Lebanon.<br /><br />And the story takes up from here: <br /><br />Adam, who refused to ever visit his country, decides to stay for a few days in the country that he thought has failed him. An old crush re-enlightens, and a project of a friends-reunion will change not only the current life and future of Adam, but also the life of the other friends. <br /><br />In this masterpiece, Adam and his other friends revisit the past and discover more about themselves, and the country that never actually left them. <br /><br />This book is about nostalgia to one's own country. About forgiving this country, and seeking forgiveness back and making peace with it. And about how your country has always been awaiting for your arrival, with open arms.<br /><br />This book is a wild, heartwarming journey, with powerful, magnificent, and flawless prose by one of my top favorite authors Amin Maalouf, who is an author, I am proud to say, from my country. <br /><br />The expressed emotions of our characters over themes like immigration from one's mother country, patriotic identity, and the life-shattering consequences of the Lebanese Civil War, seem very personal and relatable, since Amin Maalouf himself has left Lebanon to France during the war.<br /><br />In conclusion, the ending broke my heart into tiny, little pieces, but the book overall changed my views over my country, and readjusted my relationship with Lebanon to a higher level than before.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14398714520363581938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3279579620?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/1616058-annie">Annie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3279579620" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4667830838864071166">I sometimes worry that I spend too much time thinking about the meaning of titles, especially with literary fiction. They’re riddles I can’t resist. So, as I read <i>The Disoriented</i>, by Amin Maalouf (and excellently translated by Frank Wynne), I wondered what it meant to mean to be disoriented. Was Maalouf playing with the idea of being lost? Making one’s way through life without a map? Or was he taking it a step further and trading on the idea of what it means to be oriental? I saw evidence of all</span>
  <span id="freeText4667830838864071166" style="display:none">I sometimes worry that I spend too much time thinking about the meaning of titles, especially with literary fiction. They’re riddles I can’t resist. So, as I read <i>The Disoriented</i>, by Amin Maalouf (and excellently translated by Frank Wynne), I wondered what it meant to mean to be disoriented. Was Maalouf playing with the idea of being lost? Making one’s way through life without a map? Or was he taking it a step further and trading on the idea of what it means to be oriental? I saw evidence of all of these as I read, but I was left to draw my own conclusions about identity, about paths through life, about obligations—much like the characters in <i>The Disoriented</i>...<br /><br /><i>Read the rest of my review at <a href="https://abookishtype.wordpress.com/2020/04/15/the-disoriented-by-amin-maalouf/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Bookish Type</a>. I received a free copy of this book from the publisher via Edelweiss, for review consideration.</i></span>

<div id="review_2510164668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2510164668" />
    <a title="Ahmed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50267833-ahmed"><img alt="Ahmed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485981265p2/50267833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2510164668?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmed" href="/user/show/50267833-ahmed">Ahmed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9782246772712" href="/book/show/16034631-les-d-sorient-s">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2510164668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8818620100458014027">"It is our fate to be betrayed," he noted. "By our beliefs, our friends, our bodies; by life, by History..."<br/><br/>I’ve developed quite a taste for Maalouf’s novels, and this is perhaps unlike anything I’ve previously read from him. It’s more echoing, in a sense, because it is closer to my period and to that of my contemporaries. Literature, that goes without saying, need not be contemporary in theme and subject to be resonant, but when it is so, it leaves an additional mark that deeply speaks to us. I</span>
  <span id="freeText8818620100458014027" style="display:none">"It is our fate to be betrayed," he noted. "By our beliefs, our friends, our bodies; by life, by History..."<br /><br />I’ve developed quite a taste for Maalouf’s novels, and this is perhaps unlike anything I’ve previously read from him. It’s more echoing, in a sense, because it is closer to my period and to that of my contemporaries. Literature, that goes without saying, need not be contemporary in theme and subject to be resonant, but when it is so, it leaves an additional mark that deeply speaks to us. I come from a part of the world where exile happens on a daily basis. People leave, and they leave everyday abandoning everything behind them for that long-sought and now, perhaps, tired ‘better life.’ <br /><br />While I’ve said Maalouf departs a little bit from his previous history-based novels, this does have the remnants of history all over its pages. History, in Maalouf, moulds us flesh and blood. Adam, a Franco-Lebanese living in Paris, goes back to his native country that he left “after the War.” He goes back to his native soil to attend the funerals of his long-time, but separated friend, Mourad. The two friends were on bad terms because of their contention on what leaving the country and staying means. Mourad did stay, but at a terrible price. War does things to people; it summons the darkest ways in oneself, and Adam never really forgave his friend’s rite of passage. The funeral serves as an opportunity to call back all the old friends that formed a group called ‘les Byzantins,’ and it’d be Adam’s mission to reunite the group. <br /><br />Nietzsche tells us that there’s “only a perspective knowing.” That we have different intakes and commentaries; that we circle around things. Les désoriontés is a fine example of a perspectival story. Maalouf, in revisiting his character’s memory fragments and bringing together long-separated friends, gives depth to an intricate story of soil. We’re not frozen in Adam’s insight (which spells out quite explicitly his disdain for war and the failure of his country), and if we were, it would have been incredibly limited and reductive. Maalouf brilliantly draws different lines and parallels. He leaves no stone unturned, and no character voiceless. While we’re not plunged into the interior in a Faulknerian way, we do have an insight of all characters’ ideals and beliefs. These range from war, soil, nationalism to life, love and religion. Everyone has a say. <br /><br />How the book ends is perhaps the passage which moves us most. I, myself, don’t like happy endings as I never had any taste for those. There’s a fatality and melancholy in less joyous ends that render the works kind of numinous, kind of elevated… something to be found that gives the text a perenniality in the reader’s mind—a dazzling quality you find in Maalouf’s work, and Les Désorientés, perhaps, perpetuates it even more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8818620100458014027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2582566244?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elif Cakir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elif Cakir" href="/user/show/38666837-elif-cakir">Elif Cakir</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2582566244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9692404695357054031">I think only a person raised in the "non-Western" world and more specifically in Eastern Meditarrenean region could truly appreciate the value of this book. Having worked with Syrian refugees, I have always wondered how they felt about their choice to leave Syria when some of their close relatives and friends decided to remain. I found this book right in the middle of these thoughts, as if to answer my questions. How the decision to leave or stay during the civil war in Lebanon tore families and</span>
  <span id="freeText9692404695357054031" style="display:none">I think only a person raised in the "non-Western" world and more specifically in Eastern Meditarrenean region could truly appreciate the value of this book. Having worked with Syrian refugees, I have always wondered how they felt about their choice to leave Syria when some of their close relatives and friends decided to remain. I found this book right in the middle of these thoughts, as if to answer my questions. How the decision to leave or stay during the civil war in Lebanon tore families and friends apart, not only geographically, but also morally, was very well expressed by Amin Maalouf. Also, the stories of characters from different religions were a beautiful reference to the multicultural Lebanon, but also ultimately the Ottoman Empire. I was as excited as the characters whenever they engaged in a discussion about religion, the view of the Western world about the East, the dilemma of Jews from the Arab world, revolutions, the rise of radical Islam, ethics in times of war...<br />Perhaps "Les desorientes" fascinated me because I read it the right time, nonetheless I do not see why others would not appreciate it as much as I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9692404695357054031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1647860529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1647860529" />
    <a title="Bassel Alhaffar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20253237-bassel-alhaffar"><img alt="Bassel Alhaffar" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1647860529?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bassel Alhaffar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bassel Alhaffar" href="/user/show/20253237-bassel-alhaffar">Bassel Alhaffar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1647860529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6621522808030655256">Another Novel by the same writer - recommended by my friend Hassan-, which reflects on the writer's personal events carried after he came back for a visit. It's a journey were you travel to the past & live the current events with him.</span>
  <span id="freeText6621522808030655256" style="display:none">Another Novel by the same writer - recommended by my friend Hassan-, which reflects on the writer's personal events carried after he came back for a visit. It's a journey were you travel to the past &amp; live the current events with him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6621522808030655256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3389772818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23246047-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3389772818?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/23246047-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781642860580" href="/book/show/49221187-the-disoriented">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3389772818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8929882851820079324">This work is a Big Chill type story that takes places in an unnamed country in the Middle East. I I believe the location is meant to be Syria. The Levant frequently referred to in this book which was the name for the Middle East before it was artificially cut up into countries post WWI. Told in alternating chapters in first person narrative by Adam an expat who lives in France and an omniscient narrator. This is very effective in this work. The friends are trying to reassemble after the death of</span>
  <span id="freeText8929882851820079324" style="display:none">This work is a Big Chill type story that takes places in an unnamed country in the Middle East. I I believe the location is meant to be Syria. The Levant frequently referred to in this book which was the name for the Middle East before it was artificially cut up into countries post WWI. Told in alternating chapters in first person narrative by Adam an expat who lives in France and an omniscient narrator. This is very effective in this work. The friends are trying to reassemble after the death of one of the group who were fast friends in high school and college. Their backgrounds and diaspora around the world are very representative of what has happened in the Middle East post WWII to present. The story is very engaging and I gained a new perspective on the lives of the occupants of that part of the world and what has caused some to leave and some to stay. It is extremely readable and the work takes twists and turns not obvious.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8929882851820079324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4411559-anja"><img alt="Anja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348015334p2/4411559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3546387318?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja" href="/user/show/4411559-anja">Anja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781642860580" href="/book/show/49221187-the-disoriented">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3546387318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9317665850362107949">Amin Maalouf powerfully depicts the dissolution and implosion of a complex society, one which was predicated on maintaining a delicate balance within and remaining apart from geopolitical stressors. Of course no society is immune to this, so this story of unraveling is universal as it takes place in communities and nations across the globe over and over and over. On a more micro level he unpicks the tension between those who can leave and those who have to or opt to stay. His analysis of the com</span>
  <span id="freeText9317665850362107949" style="display:none">Amin Maalouf powerfully depicts the dissolution and implosion of a complex society, one which was predicated on maintaining a delicate balance within and remaining apart from geopolitical stressors. Of course no society is immune to this, so this story of unraveling is universal as it takes place in communities and nations across the globe over and over and over. On a more micro level he unpicks the tension between those who can leave and those who have to or opt to stay. His analysis of the compromises each makes to survive and thrive in an imperfect world left me in awe. And lastly his depiction of lives in our early twenties when everything is still possible and then applying the lens back from the future is heartbreaking. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9317665850362107949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2747930865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2747930865" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47630228-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444673993p2/47630228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2747930865?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/47630228-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789044535952" href="/book/show/34225007-de-ontheemden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47630228-inge?shelf=novel">novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2747930865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10140958342797321416">Beautiful and thought provoking novel. Both perspectives - the third person narrative and the correspondence/diary first person pieces - give an unique insight into the thoughts and actions of Adam, a historian living in Paris who returns to the country of his birth for the first time in over two decades. Both points of view offer often very touching insights on why and when someone decides to leave his home country behind. Nothing is truly black and white, and depending what -and even more impo</span>
  <span id="freeText10140958342797321416" style="display:none">Beautiful and thought provoking novel. Both perspectives - the third person narrative and the correspondence/diary first person pieces - give an unique insight into the thoughts and actions of Adam, a historian living in Paris who returns to the country of his birth for the first time in over two decades. Both points of view offer often very touching insights on why and when someone decides to leave his home country behind. Nothing is truly black and white, and depending what -and even more importantly - whom they leave behind if they do go, clearly has influenced all the friends' decisions. <br />The strength of this book is Adam's unique way of looking at things though - a historian through and through, he dissects the events of long ago to tell the unique story of his friends - and of himself. However he does not stop his analysis with looking into the facts, he understands that feelings are as important, that they cloud judgement -his as much as that of his friends. A wonderful story, with a most unsettling ending. All in all an impressive novel, that i will not easily forget!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10140958342797321416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2506169153" />
    <a title="Frank Kool" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82232815-frank-kool"><img alt="Frank Kool" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562439262p2/82232815.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2506169153?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frank Kool" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frank Kool" href="/user/show/82232815-frank-kool">Frank Kool</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789044526196" href="/book/show/20497123-de-ontheemden">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2506169153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16003603048841217573"><i>Les Désorientés</i> is a novel, mostly narrated through letters and diary entries, about the reunion of old friends from the Levant who all went their separate way through life following a tragic event. It is also beautifully written.<br/><br/>That is as short and precise a summary I would make of it. Despite the many story-lines intersecting each other, it is easy to read due to the short chapters and the beautiful prose. One gripe about the conversation: sometimes it feels a bit unnatural because there is s</span>
  <span id="freeText16003603048841217573" style="display:none"><i>Les Désorientés</i> is a novel, mostly narrated through letters and diary entries, about the reunion of old friends from the Levant who all went their separate way through life following a tragic event. It is also beautifully written.<br /><br />That is as short and precise a summary I would make of it. Despite the many story-lines intersecting each other, it is easy to read due to the short chapters and the beautiful prose. One gripe about the conversation: sometimes it feels a bit unnatural because there is so much eloquence and poetry in their everyday speak. Additionally, sometimes characters will tell each other details about historical events that should be common knowledge anyone from that region.<br /><br />Perhaps it makes more sense to read the book as if it were a play: the dialogue may feel unnatural at times, but it is very poignant and there is more than enough to unpack between the lines. Interspersed between the discussions about politics and romantic relationships, there are some beautiful and even <i>beautifully sad</i> episodes. There's irony abound as well, such as the delightful story of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the man who was about to kill himself, but was cured of his suicidal tendencies after being abducted and befriending his captors <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />What I liked is that Maalouf lets you get to know the characters before he labels them. Needless to say, there is a lot of weight put on classifications like which religion, ethnicity, or political affiliation applies to each individual, but the book goes on for quite some length before you know who's the Muslim/Jew/Atheist/Christian/whathaveyou. Maalouf is not about to pass final judgment on any issue. Rather, he would like that each get a fair hearing. As such, the various characters become mouth-pieces for all different sides, be it Zionism, Islamism, nationalism, pacifism, humanism, or pan-Arabism.<br /><br />Those who have read Maalouf's <i>Disordered World</i> (which I highly recommend) may recognize some of his views on politics and history. Perhaps most striking is that he rejects the notion of a 'clash of cultures', but rather sees it as an 'exhaustion of cultures', with the Middle-East as the cutting edge where the flaws of Western and Muslim culture(s) become most apparent.<br />In fact, these two books can be seen as two sides of the same coin: DW giving you the historical outlines and data, while LD puts a human face on 'mere' history.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16003603048841217573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3570924821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3570924821" />
    <a title="Nour Bou Salman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/81461388-nour-bou-salman"><img alt="Nour Bou Salman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575729881p2/81461388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3570924821?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nour Bou Salman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nour Bou Salman" href="/user/show/81461388-nour-bou-salman">Nour Bou Salman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3570924821&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3570924821" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6264168494952599302">I was super busy for months that I didn't have the time to read any book. This is why I needed something strong enough to get me back on track, and this masterpiece didn't disappoint me. I may be a little biased because Amin here narrates the story of young Lebanese friends detaching from each other, their country, and their happy lives, due to all the shit Lebanon was passing through back in the 70s and 80s.<br/>I read it in Arabic, my favorite language, which recently started to need more attention</span>
  <span id="freeText6264168494952599302" style="display:none">I was super busy for months that I didn't have the time to read any book. This is why I needed something strong enough to get me back on track, and this masterpiece didn't disappoint me. I may be a little biased because Amin here narrates the story of young Lebanese friends detaching from each other, their country, and their happy lives, due to all the shit Lebanon was passing through back in the 70s and 80s.<br />I read it in Arabic, my favorite language, which recently started to need more attention from me, and below are my favorite quotes:<br /><br />١ - «في هذه الضيعة؛ لا نعرف المسلم من اليهودي من المسيحي. اليس كذلك؟». كان والدي يوافقه الرأي بإيماءة من الرأس. وبالطبع، لم يكن ذلك صحيحاً، ولا أحد منهما يجهل ذلك. وحين نلتقي أحدهم في الشارع، نعرف دوماً، وغريزياً، إلى أي طائفة ينتمي، إنما كان يطيب سماع هذا الكلام، لأن النية كانت سليمة».<br /><br />٢ - لم اكف عن متابعة كل ما يجري في البلد عن كثب، الا اني اقلعت نهائيا عن التفكير في العودة اليه. لم اكن اقول ابدا:"لن اعود اليه"؛ بل كنت اقول:"فيما بعد"، "ليس هذا الصيف"، "ربما السنة القادمة". وفي اعماقي، كنت اعلل النفس، بشيء من الخيلاء، بألا اعود للاستقرار في البلد الا حين يعود كما عهدته من قبل. كنت ادري ان هذا الامر مستحيل، و لكن هذا الشرط لم يكن قابلا للمساومة، ولا يزال كذلك.<br />ذلك هو اسلوبي في الوفاء، ولم اشأ ان اتبمى اسلوبا آخراً على الاطلاق.<br />و ادرك اصدقائي مع مرور الوقت بأني لن اعود. و كتب لي بعضهم، منهم لاستصواب قراري، و منهم لاسماعي المواعظ.<br /><br />٣ - لوددت أن يكون لكلماتي تأثير عليك. لوددت لو تفلح كلماتي في اقناعك بأن تتسامح مع هذا البلد، ان تتقبله كما هو. سيكون دوماً بلد الاحزاب، و الفوضى، و المحسوبيات، و المحاباة و والفساد.<br />و لكنه كذلك بلد العيش الرغيد، والدفء الإنساني، والكرم، وبلد أعز اصدقائك.<br />و من الصفات الحميدة الأخرى لبلدنا أن بوسع المرء فيه العيش في واحة من اللامبالاة. فحتى حين تشتعل جميع احياء المدينة، تبقى ضيعتنا، و دارنا العتيقة، و شرفتنا الفسيحة كما عرفتها؛ يوافينا بعض الأصدقاء اليها بين الحين والآخر، كما في الماضي. و بعضهم الآخر كف عن المجيء، وسنظل نشتاق إليهم، و ضعفي يوحي لي بأنهم يشتاقون قليلاً إلينا كذلك.<br /><br />٤ - «بلى، مراد، كانت الحياة ستكون جميلة لو لم تندلع الحرب، لو ما زلنا في العشرين عوضاً عن الخمسين، لو لم يمت أي واحد منا، لو لم يخن أي واحد منا، لو لم يتغرب اي منا، لو ظل بلدنا لؤلوة الشرق، لو لم نصبح أضحوكة العالم وهاجسه وفزاعته و كبش فدائه، لو، ولو، ولو، ولو...».</span>

This book reveal a deep humanist thought on humans and their belonging to one country / one community. Ove</span>
  <span id="freeText5002357814993515451" style="display:none">This was my first time reading one of Amin Maalouf’s book and I had high expectations toward Les désorientés. I wasn’t disappointed at all ! This book reveal a deep humanist thought on humans and their belonging to one country / one community. Furthermore, regarding the recent context in Lebanon, this books gives you a better understanding on how the Lebanese people have been suffering since decades from the corruption in their country along with a sense of helplessness toward the situation. Overall I’ll keep in mind one of Amin Maalouf sentence that illustrates it pretty well : « De la disparition du passé on s’en remet facilement, c’est de la disparition de l’avenir dont on ne se remet pas. »</span>

  <span id="freeText17851852733368009375" style="display:none">One of the most beautiful stories I've ever read. <br /><br />Adam returned to his hometown in Libanon when he heard that his former best friend Mourad was dying. Many of them fled, some stayed on to make a profit out of the war, most of them lost their idealism. <span id="freeTextContainer16428534837059975559">Deep, intense and beautiful book about friends who got reunited after being forced to leave their home country, Lebanon, because of the war and other unfortunate events. It is a mixture of diary notes and storytelling of their nostalgies, sensitive discussions and disagreements and another way of reading the story and struggles of Middle Eastern countries. Highly recommended! </span>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_2501458'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2501458._"><img alt="ذاكرة الجسد" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1291756684l/2501458._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vIdioWGmTF2s5KJOs2VD52xzSi68OPQ+R91pV/onwjaGoQtz2viFNQvPFi9EkEk4uiyt5nK1elkcoy/mN2QwrA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QP0YOuzpgka+tEiguyuD4ws6NFmqKyqdSYUXN1yXoZ9623HoV7dLLhmf/MFM3ok83WXTkWSmpPoS+1GGkdRTBQ==')})
  }

</script>

احتدام الصراع المسلّح بين النظام السوري والأخوان المسلمين. يعود “مصطفى خليفة” إلى بلاده من فرنسا، بعد حصوله على إجازة في الإخراج السينمائي. “بلادي (سوريا) بحاجة إليّ أكثر من أي دولة أُخْرَى”. وهكذا كان. يترك مصطفى خلفه كل شيء: صديقته، مقاهي باريس، حقوق الإنسان، البيرة، وأشياء أُخْرَى.. يصل إلى المطار. يوقفه الأمن السوري. يأخذوه إلى التحقيق، بتهمة الانتماء إلى تنظيم “الإخوان المسلمين”، علماً انه مسيحي حسب الهويّة، وملحد في المعتقد. وهناك، يختفي مصطفى لمدّة 13 سنة، ثلاثة أشهر وثلاثة عشرة يوماً، في سجون النظام.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"13171203115799281307\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/36378.Amin_Maalouf">About Amin Maalouf</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/36378.Amin_Maalouf"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1426326347p3/36378.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/36378.Amin_Maalouf">Amin Maalouf
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,632
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10956907504133706661">Amin Maalouf (Arabic: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4456125' rel='nofollow noopener'>أمين معلوف</a>; alternate spelling <i>Amin Maluf</i>) is a Lebanese journalist and novelist. He writes and publishes primarily in French.<br/><br/>Most of Maalouf's books have a historical setting, and like Umberto Eco, Orhan Pamuk, and Arturo Pérez-Reverte, Maalouf mixes fascinating historical facts with fantasy and philosophical ideas. In an interview Maalouf has said that his role as a writer </span>
  <span id="freeText10956907504133706661" style="display:none">Amin Maalouf (Arabic: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4456125" rel="nofollow noopener">أمين معلوف</a>; alternate spelling <i>Amin Maluf</i>) is a Lebanese journalist and novelist. He writes and publishes primarily in French.<br /><br />Most of Maalouf's books have a historical setting, and like Umberto Eco, Orhan Pamuk, and Arturo Pérez-Reverte, Maalouf mixes fascinating historical facts with fantasy and philosophical ideas. In an interview Maalouf has said that his role as a writer is to create "positive myths". Maalouf's works, written with the skill of a master storyteller, offer a sensitive view of the values and attitudes of different cultures in the Middle East, Africa and Mediterranean world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10956907504133706661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/21806705-les-d-sorient-s">Quotes from التائهون</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;لستُ من أتباع أي دين، ولا أشعر بالحاجة لأن أصبح كذلك. <br />وموقفي من هذه المسألة غير مريح لا سيما وأنني لا أشعر بنفسي ملحدًا كذلك. لا أستطيع أن أؤمن بأن السماء فارغة، وبأنه لا يوجد بعد الموت سوى العدم. فماذا يوجد وراء ذلك؟ لا أدري. هل يوجد شيء ما؟ لا علم لي. أرجو ذلك، إنما لا أعرف؛ وأشعر بالريبة إزاء من يدعون المعرفة، سواء كانت أشكال يقينهم دينية أم ملحدة. <br />إنني في منزلة بين الإيمان وعدم الإيمان مثلما أنا في منزلة بين وطنين، ألاطف هذا وألاطف ذاك، ولا أنتمي لأي منهما. لا أشعر بنفسي غير مؤمن إلا حين أستمع إلى عظة رجل دين؛ ففي كل عظة، وكل إشارة إلى كتاب مقدس، يتمرد عقلي، ويتشتت انتباهي، وتتمتم شفتاي لعنات. غير أني أرتعش في أعماقي حين أحضر مأتمًا علمانيًا، وتتملكني الرغبة بدندنة تراتيل سريانية، أو بيزنطية، أو حتى ترتيلة القربان المقدس القديمة التي يقال إنها من تأليف توما الأكويني. <br />ذلك هو درب التيه الذي أسلكه في مجال الدين. وبالطبع، أسير فيه وحيدًا، بدون أن أتبع أحدًا، وبدون أن أدعو أحدًا لأن يتبعني.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/741478">189 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
